  <div class="page-section--sidebar page-section container" id="main-post">
   <div class="page-section-content">
    <div class="post">
     <h1>
      What bartenders actually think of your drink order
     </h1>
     <div class="post-inner clearfix">
      <div class="post-meta">
       <div class="post-meta-author">
        by
        <a href="http://matadornetwork.com/author/lisamillarjones/">
         Lisa Millar-Jones
        </a>
       </div>
       <div class="post-meta-date">
        November 20, 2014
       </div>
       <div class="post-avatar">
        <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-100" height="100" src="http://cdn1.matadornetwork.com/assets/images/authors/lisamillarjones.jpg" width="100"/>
       </div>
       <div class="post-share-wrapper post-share--vertical" data-post-id="265696" data-sticky="" data-sticky-max-width="991" data-sticky-offset-top="69" data-sticky-parent-contain="" data-sticky-parent-selector=".page-section">
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="post-content">
       <div class="wp-caption aligncenter" id="attachment_265698" style="width: 610px">
        <a href="http://cdn1.matadornetwork.com/blogs/1/2014/11/bartender-drink-order.jpg">
         <noscript>
          <img alt="bartender-drink-order" src="http://cdn1.matadornetwork.com/blogs/1/2014/11/bartender-drink-order.jpg" title=""/>
         </noscript>
         <img class="size-full wp-image-265698 lazy" data-original="http://cdn1.matadornetwork.com/blogs/1/2014/11/bartender-drink-order.jpg" height="399" src="http://cdn1.matadornetwork.com/assets/images/blank1.png" width="600"/>
        </a>
        <p class="wp-caption-text">
         (
         <a href="http://capricenightclub.thisisblueprint.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/5/2014/10/post/bartender-confessions-what-we-think-about-your-drink-of-choice/elite-daily-girls-drinking.jpg">
          via
         </a>
         )
        </p>
       </div>
       <p>
        <span style="text-transform:uppercase;">
         Forget your haircut, the clothes
        </span>
        youre wearing, and your body language; believe it or not, your bartender can tell everything about you by what you order at the bar. Here is what your drink order says about you (according to your bartender):
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Goose &amp; Cranberry (or Red Bull):
        </strong>
        You dont know what youre doing.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Whiskey, neat:
        </strong>
        Youre hot.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Jger Bombs:
        </strong>
        If you are a male, you miss your frat boys. If you are a female, you have low self-esteem that can only be appeased by sex with a stranger.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Old-Fashioned:
        </strong>
        You recognize the value in hard work, and hold the reward for that hard work in high regard.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Baileys on the rocks:
        </strong>
        You still live at home with your parents.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Moscato:
        </strong>
        Youre just ordering this cause you heard it in a Drake song (p.s. it is a sweet Italian wine).
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Bacardi 151 for a friends:
        </strong>
        Youre a dick.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Bacardi 151 for yourself:
        </strong>
        Theres something wrong with you.
       </p>
       <div class="pullquote-center">
        <noscript>
         <img alt="" src="http://cdn1.matadornetwork.com/assets/images/site/matador-logo-small.png" title=""/>
        </noscript>
        <img class=" lazy" data-original="http://cdn1.matadornetwork.com/assets/images/site/matador-logo-small.png" src="http://cdn1.matadornetwork.com/assets/images/blank1.png"/>
        <em>
         More like this
         <a href="http://matadornetwork.com/nights/bartenders-actually-think-beer-selection/" target="_blank" title="What bartenders actually think of your beer selection">
          What bartenders actually think of your beer selection
         </a>
        </em>
       </div>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Demand something free:
        </strong>
        You are with a group of squealing girls wearing tiaras and/or matching shirts and will tip poorly (if at all).
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Long Island Iced Tea:
        </strong>
        Your ID is fake and you are here to get white-girl wasted.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Apple-Tini:
        </strong>
        You hate the taste of alcohol.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Whatevers cheap:
        </strong>
        (In my head: you!). This is an sign that you wont be tipping either.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Jameson:
        </strong>
        You know what youre doing.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Cosmopolitan:
        </strong>
        Youre aging, lack imagination, and have watched too much SATC.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         White Russian:
        </strong>
        You have never worked in a bar before, so you have a fool-hearted confidence that the milk in the cooler is not expired.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Shot of  well Tequila:
        </strong>
        You are emotionally unstable.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Don Julio on the rocks:
        </strong>
        You too know what youre doing.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Patron Margarita:
        </strong>
        You wish to spend $15 on a drink that will taste exactly the same as a $7 drink.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Champagne for everyone:
        </strong>
        You have too much money and dont know what to do with it.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Hennessy and Coke:
        </strong>
        Can you guys play some rap music?
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         PBR:
        </strong>
        Hipsters dont tip.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Alize in a snifter:
        </strong>
        Oh, you (think youre) fancy, huh?
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Amaretto sour:
        </strong>
        Youre a female who never knew what to order, so a bartender made it for you once and now you order it all the time because its the only drink you know how to order.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         1 Candy Apple, 2 Porn Stars, 1 Sour Jack:
        </strong>
        Are you fucking with me?! You are the bane of my existence.
       </p>
       <div class="pullquote-center">
        <noscript>
         <img alt="" src="http://cdn1.matadornetwork.com/assets/images/site/matador-logo-small.png" title=""/>
        </noscript>
        <img class=" lazy" data-original="http://cdn1.matadornetwork.com/assets/images/site/matador-logo-small.png" src="http://cdn1.matadornetwork.com/assets/images/blank1.png"/>
        <em>
         More like this
         <a href="http://matadornetwork.com/nights/53-things-youre-totally-annoy-bartender/" target="_blank" title="53 things you're doing that totally annoy the bartender">
          53 things you're doing that totally annoy the bartender
         </a>
        </em>
       </div>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Gin &amp; Juice:
        </strong>
        Sure buddy, is Snoop Dogg shooting a music video in here that Im not aware of?
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         A Hi-Ball:
        </strong>
        Its your first time in a bar, you heard they were on special, but you have no idea what a hi-ball is. But you still ask the bartender for  a Hi-Ball.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Caesar:
        </strong>
        Youre hungover.
       </p>
       <p>
        <strong>
         Bottle of Ros:
        </strong>
        You cry during sex.
       </p>
       <p>
        <em>
         Compiled by Lisa Millar-Jones from the bartenders at
         <a href="http://www.capricenightclub.com/">
          Caprice Nightclub
         </a>
         and
         <a href="http://capricenightclub.com/news/bartender-confessions-what-we-think-about-your-drink-of-choice">
          republished
         </a>
         by permission.
        </em>
       </p>

            <p>
             secondly, i was a waitress for years and dabbled in bartending, and I will let you know that that was the best job I ever had. Yes, you deal with a lot of shitty people and situations, but you do get to meet amazing people (clearly you not being one of them), and you do actually build ALL the real-life skills you need to function in the world SUCH AS: working with and for a diverse population, patience and self-control in unnerving situations, quick problem-solving skills when the inevitable occurs,  working with others for the greater good (i.e not having a restaurant full of pissed off customers), presenting yourself in a clean, pleasant manner to others, multitasking in an efficient manner to work smarter, not harder.and I can keep rambling if you want.
            </p>
            <p>
             In case you are wondering, I did this job while attending college full-time. I am now a teacher, (yes, some of us DO become real professionals and leave this environmentwe are not ALL stagnant there) and I can tell you that the waitressing/bartending job is what really prepared me for the real-world, not sitting in a fucking office when I was a dental assistant.(Sounds fancier, right? But when the fuck else will I have to mix cement, or develop x-rays, or sterilize equipment again?                 </p>
               </div>
              </div>
             </li>

                  <p>
                   Okay, Mr. Bartender, heres a fairly simple problem that most people with a years experience in networking should be able to solve: 2 data centres with their own ARIN IP ranges.  Both connected to the same set of providers under the same registry since theyre the same company.  Default route was removed from the BGP routers at one of the data centres.  Now, anything inside either DC can communicate with anything on the internet except the other data centre.  So, either explain to me what happened, or how to fix it.
                  </p>
                  <p>
                   point is, bartending can only prepare you for jobs that dont require any sort of technical knowledge like IT, engineering, accounting, or even HR.  It can only prepare you for jobs that dont require any hard skills but put a premium on social skills, such as sales.
                  </p>

                  </p>
                  <p>
                   Ive bartended full-time for years and now just one night a week on the side of my career.  I still love bartending. Its like a night out for me with great pay, gets me away from the office, and a little bonus pay.
                  </p>
                  <p>
                   With all that being said, at this point, I could buy or partner into my own establishment if I chose. Due to the long hours and having a young child, a bar/restaurant is not my choice anymore, event planning services will be top priority. The weddings, mitzvahs  ave over $20,000 per event for a good planner. Guess what gave me those skills?  Bartending and my current career job as operations manager for the US top paid photographer!  Bartending gave me the organization skills, people skills, etc. the clientele whom Im in with right now will land me the most upscale references for my next step!  Why start at the bottom?  Because Ive chosen the top!  Its all a mindset little ones!  Great things will come to those that work hard, plan well, and know their roots!  Wishing all the bartenders of America a fabulous day!! xoxo

             <li class="comment even depth-4" id="dsq-comment-191985">
              <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-191985">
               <cite id="dsq-cite-191985">
                <span id="dsq-author-user-191985">
                 Chris Tharp
                </span>
               </cite>
              </div>
              <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-191985">
               <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-191985">
                <p>
                 I was just making a snarky comment. Ive been to Japan a few times (I live next door in Korea) and have drunk there mightily, though I cant really comment on the strength of the cocktails since I pretty much only drink beer. I kind of agree with you about how American bartending is overrated. Every time I go home I am struck by just how many bartenders are power-tripping, arrogant, entitled fucks. Not all of them, mind you. But a lot of them expect a big tip for splashing some ale in a glass or mixing two liquids together and seem to have a chip on their shoulder. I always tip, mind you (a buck a beer, a buck whiskey when I indulge) but raise my eyebrows every time I hear American service staff moaning about making minimum wage while also boasting about walking with hundreds a night. I understand that dealing with drunks can get old, but after a decade of living abroad, I realize that the barstaff in much of the world offers much less attitude, even when theyre taking home a fraction of what some bartenders clear back home. Its almost as if more money turns people into bigger assholes. Imagine that.
                </p>
               </div>
              </div>

           Im a bartender, there are 3 other bars that are popular like mine. Oh wait that is over half the bill! Yea no. I make $300-$400 a night when Im behind the bar and $200-$300 when waitressing. Not counting if Im a double Ill make $400-$600 because our restaurant is so busy.  I make about $1,500- $2,000 a week. Im 21 and I know thats damn good money for someone my age. Is it something I want to do for the rest of my life, no. Do I enjoy it? Yes.

       <li class="comment even thread-even depth-1" id="dsq-comment-192311">
        <div class="dsq-comment-header" id="dsq-comment-header-192311">
         <cite id="dsq-cite-192311">
          <span id="dsq-author-user-192311">
           BillyBar
          </span>
         </cite>
        </div>
        <div class="dsq-comment-body" id="dsq-comment-body-192311">
         <div class="dsq-comment-message" id="dsq-comment-message-192311">
          <p>
           To the negative people. Ill simply share my life.
          </p>
          <p>
           Im 30, male. Im a bartender for 10 years and counting. Ive made 50-120k a year, depending on venues through those years. I wake up at 10am. Drive to do my errands in NO TRAFFIC. Have the day to go to the beach, do some shopping, play some golf etc, which, I do. In slow season, I go overseas for a few months. I drive to work around 7pm, in NO TRAFFIC. I get to work and people are happy to see me and I am the boss. Not really, the boss, Im simply an employee. But, its my house and as the bartender, I am in charge. It is difficult work and many people cant handle the pressure, but its challenging and pushes ME through obstacles that make me grow. I easy spend under $1000 a year on going out. Most places I go, are free. And due to my job, im fit  Im not taking a stab at 9-5ers, Im simply stating my reality. This is my life. It probably sounds farfetched to some. Others will completely understand and relate.
          </p>
          <p>
           9-5 is safe for most people. Linear income. Thats great. Cash jobs, to a smart person, open up new doors
          </p>
          <p>
           Thanks directly to bartending, I have 7 homes paid off (small investment, single family homes), and a small, 6 unit strip mall, nearly paid off. I know thousands of people who have invited me to thier homes domestically and internationally resulting in countless vacations with absolutely minimal expense on my end.
          </p>
          <p>
           With a family, sure, this may not be an ideal job. With age, it may be hard to keep up with the demands of the job. If you are into drugs and are an alcoholic, not the best environment and you will be 50 and still there (With that said I know dozens of 50+ year olds at 5 star steakhouses making in the 125k+ ballpark). BUT, bartending will retire me in 2 years due to properly invested income. And retire means, earning above 75k a year in rents. Ill still do something. I enjoy work!!!
          </p>
          <p>
           This last line may get some criticism, but, ill get it no matter what.
          </p>
          <p>
           Hospitality taught me how to survive. How to move. How to hussle. Now, while great for some such as doctors and lawyers, College, for most, is a waste of time and money. College does not teach you how to make money and due to the ridiculous student loan programs out there, many students will be in their mid 30s before they can be debt free. And the rejects will end up in hospitality.
          </p>
          <p>
           Im one of those rejects and Im so proud of it. What ever you do, if you are a bartender or in an office, just make sure
           <br/>
           you truly enjoy it. If you DONT, then you are living this life
           <br/>
           incorrectly. Haters, your turn.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>

                    nodes[i].parentNode.setAttribute('data-disqus-identifier', nodes[i].getAttribute('data-dsqidentifier'));
                    url = nodes[i].parentNode.href.split('#', 1);
                    if (url.length == 1) { url = url[0]; }
                    else { url = url[1]; }
                    nodes[i].parentNode.href = url + '#disqus_thread';
                }
            }
            var s = document.createElement('script'); 
            s.async = true;
            s.type = 'text/javascript';
            s.src = '//' + disqus_shortname + '.disqus.com/count.js';
            (document.getElementsByTagName('HEAD')[0] || document.getElementsByTagName('BODY')[0]).appendChild(s);
        }());
        // ]]&gt;
  </script>
